Negotiations on French Legal Rights 124

National Federation of Commerce Sends Telegram Urging Strict Warning

The National Federation of Commerce yesterday sent a telegram to the National Government Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that it had been approved by the Taiyuan Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The telegram opened by stating, "Since our country promulgated an order in February of the 18th year of the Republic (1929) to abolish consular jurisdiction from January of the 19th year (1930), among the countries with consular jurisdiction in China, apart from those that will voluntarily abandon it or re-negotiate agreements due to the expiration of treaties, only six countries are still in negotiations. According to reports, since the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a note last December, among the six countries, the Netherlands and Norway have expressed their willingness to negotiate the abolition, Brazil is also willing to consider it, and the United Kingdom and the United States absolutely agree. It is clear that these countries have sincerity in abolishing consular jurisdiction and are gradually reaching a consensus. Only France, regarding negotiations on our legal rights, is still following the old pattern, delaying and ignoring it, and not providing a sincere response to our Ministry's note. Moreover, the French envoy's trip to the capital has been repeatedly delayed. Such deliberate delay is tantamount to disregarding our national sovereignty and abandoning friendly relations. A country's judicial system is a matter of internal affairs, and other countries have no right to interfere. Today, in the world, whether large or small, only China is bound by consular jurisdiction. Now that the National Government is determined to restore sovereignty and abolish consular jurisdiction, all compatriots across the country should vow to fight to the death to support the government and not give up until the goal is achieved. We urge you to unanimously support the National Government's diplomatic policy of abolishing consular jurisdiction and promote its realization in the shortest possible time. We share a common hatred and strongly warn France not to respect our national sovereignty. This emergency telegram cannot express our extreme indignation." Signed: Taiyuan Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Upon receipt of this, we are sending this telegram to your government and departments for review. We earnestly request that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs be swiftly instructed to conduct serious negotiations with France to protect our national rights. Respectfully, Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, with seal.

Establishment of the Shanghai Gazetteer Hall Preparatory Committee 125

Grand Meeting Held Yesterday

The Municipal Government established the Preparatory Committee for the Municipal Gazetteer Hall in June of the year before last to compile the city's gazetteer. Mayor Zhang appointed the directors of the Education, Finance, and Social Affairs Bureaus to undertake the work. Due to the heavy workload of the committee, which could not be shouldered by a few people, it was reorganized and expanded. The mayor serves as the chairman, the secretary general, and the directors of each bureau are members. Tang Jicang, Qu Xuanjing, and Zhao Zhengping were appointed as full-time members. The inaugural meeting was held at the Municipal Government Auditorium at 1:00 PM yesterday. The mayor chaired the meeting.

Meeting Agenda: (1) All stand at attention. (2) Sing the Party song. (3) Bow three times to the national flag, the Party flag, and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen. (4) The chairman respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will. (5) Three minutes of silence. (6) Chairman's speech. (7) Speeches. (8) Adjournment.

Chairman's Speech: Chairman Mayor Zhang said, "Today, the Preparatory Committee for the Municipal Gazetteer Hall is expanded and established. The first thing I want to explain is that this matter is very important and memorable for our city. Some people say that compiling a gazetteer is not an urgent matter for our city because our city has not had a long history. Some people say that compiling a gazetteer is only for the preservation and reference of literature and seems to be unrelated to practical use. Some people say that the area of this gazetteer is divided from Shanghai and Baoshan counties, and the gazetteers of these two counties were published after the establishment of the Republic of China. It seems that not much material can be collected separately since the time interval is short. There is also a saying that the Jiangsu Provincial Gazetteer is also preparing a special edition for Shanghai, so it seems unnecessary to compile a separate gazetteer for our city. These statements all seem to have some reasons, but none of them have seen the importance of compiling a gazetteer for our city. Regarding the first statement, compiling a gazetteer for our city is not to preserve the literature of the Municipal Government but to collect the literature of our city. It has nothing to do with the length of the Municipal Government's history. Regarding the second statement, compiling a gazetteer should not seek beauty but seek practicality. This is not only the understanding that modern people should have, but also Mr. Zhang Shizhai, a scholar who was very knowledgeable about compiling gazetteers, once said. Regarding the third statement, the gazetteers of Shanghai and Baoshan counties all follow the old examples of previous gazetteers. All the facts manifested in the new era can be said to have been completely ignored and not collected at all. This may be due to the limited financial resources of a county and the inability to seek perfection. Regarding the fourth statement, Jiangsu Province is a centrally-administered administrative region, and our city is also a centrally-administered administrative region. The Shanghai section should not be included in the Jiangsu Provincial Gazetteer, just as the Zhejiang Province section should not be included in the Jiangsu Provincial Gazetteer. However, the issue of whether or not to compile the Shanghai Gazetteer is another matter, and the need to compile a gazetteer for our city is a responsibility that cannot be shirked. The errors of the above statements have been explained. Now I want to talk about the important reasons for compiling a gazetteer for our city. To talk about this important reason, we must first talk about the value of national history. We often say that China is an ancient civilization of four thousand years, but where is the evidence of the ancient civilization of four thousand years? We must say that there are the Six Classics as evidence and the Twenty-Four Histories as evidence. However, Mr. Gong Ding'an said that the Six Classics are the descendants of the Zhou History. So, to put it simply, China can be called an ancient civilization of four thousand years because it has four thousand years of national history. Therefore, although the national system has changed, the national history has not been interrupted. Because the national history has not been interrupted, we can be called a country of four thousand years of antiquity. Now, although the Qing History and the founding history of the Republic of China have not yet been reviewed and published by the National Government, the National Government will eventually begin working on these two histories sooner or later. We should actively compile local gazetteers before the National Government begins to compile the history of the Republic of China. Why? Because the local gazetteer is the only important basis for selecting materials for the national history. This reason has been said by many scholars such as Gong Ding'an and Zhang Shizhai. Therefore, Gong Ding'an said that Confucius and Zuo Qiuming wrote the Spring and Autumn Annals after Zhou obtained the books of 120 countries. Sima Qian's net to gather old news from all over the world to write the Historical Records also had to be based on the Spring and Autumn Annals and the Guo Yu. So, today, the compilation of local gazetteers in various provinces and cities is the foundation for compiling the national history in the future. Especially Shanghai, in terms of economic status, is the first commercial port in the country. In terms of political and academic status, it has often been the pioneer of the country for decades. In terms of the status of the revolution, I don't know how many people's efforts and sacrifices it took to achieve today's results. Whether or not there is a detailed and applicable city gazetteer in our city is very important to the compilation of national history. Furthermore, in terms of current needs, abolishing unequal treaties is an important party program determined by our Party. The recovery of the concessions is only a matter of time. Citizens must know the horizontal and vertical aspects of our city and the special zone. Not only citizens but also people who are concerned about the national economy, national culture, and national social issues must have an in-depth study of Shanghai. A great work that can provide this kind of research can never be done by private investigation or described in detail by private writing. Because there is this important reason, it is necessary to establish a gazetteer hall. Before the establishment of the gazetteer hall, there are still many matters that should be carried out. Therefore, the Municipal Government has the need to establish a preparatory committee for the municipal gazetteer hall. It is natural for me and the Secretary-General and directors of each bureau of the Municipal Government to participate in this committee to provide information within the scope of our respective duties. In addition, we have appointed Mr. Tang Jicang, Mr. Zhao Zhengping, and Mr. Qu Xuanjing as full-time members. The three gentlemen are very knowledgeable in the study of history and are very familiar with the horizontal and vertical aspects of our city. We will surely be satisfied and happy with the progress in the future. Regarding the issue of compiling a gazetteer, I personally have one more thought. Some people say that the compilation of a gazetteer should not be too fast. It took many people's efforts to compile a Songjiang Prefecture Gazetteer a hundred years ago, and it still took five or six years. It took more than fifty years to complete the Anhui Provincial Gazetteer. The Jiangsu Gazetteer has been in progress since a special bureau was established at the end of the Qing Dynasty, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government is still continuing its work. Therefore, it is impossible to be too fast. However, Mr. Yuan Daochong compiled the Jiaozhou Gazetteer in recent times. Although it took one or two years to interview, it took only four months from the start of compilation to the completion of the book. Of course, Jiaozhou is a newly opened city without a long history. However, the speed of success of the compiler is enough to surprise the gazetteer personnel of each province. Therefore, I hope that all members of this committee will complete the preparatory matters that should be carried out by the gazetteer hall on schedule in a responsible spirit, so that the gazetteer hall can be established as soon as possible and officially compile the city's gazetteer, so that the Municipal Government can make a great and rapid contribution to the civilization of the city and the whole country. This is what I deeply hope for."

Nanshi Customhouse Not Yet Abolished 126

Due to Lack of Notification from the Ministry of Finance

Since the implementation of the abolition of likin, the regular customhouses within 50 li have not been abolished. The Ministry of Finance only recently issued an order to abolish them. The Jianghai Customhouse has had a regular customhouse within 50 li in Nanshi for a very long time. The annual tax revenue is about one million yuan. According to an important official of the Customs, the Jianghai Customhouse has not yet received a formal order from the Ministry of Finance, so the Nanshi Customhouse is still operating as usual. The closure will begin after the formal order from the Ministry arrives.

Extension of Time Limit for Transportation and Sales of Existing Yarn and Cloth Approved for Another Half Month 127

The Consolidated Tax Office Yesterday Notified the Yarn Mill Federation

The Shanghai Chinese Yarn Mill Federation previously requested an extension of the time limit for the transportation and sales of yarn and cloth stored before February 1 because it was feared that it could not be transported and sold as scheduled, and the Consolidated Tax Office granted an extension until March 31. Subsequently, in view of the sluggish sales and the pressing deadline, the Federation again requested the Consolidated Tax Office for a further extension. The Consolidated Tax Office replied that the Ministry's order did not allow for a further extension and should be complied with as scheduled. From April 1, all taxes should be supplemented, and four standards for supplementing taxes were stipulated: (1) Cotton yarn and its direct woven products manufactured before February 1 that have been shipped from the factory warehouse can be sold locally after April 1 without supplementing the consolidated tax. If they are transported from the location of the original yarn mill or weaving mill to other locations, they must pay the consolidated tax if they do not have a tax certificate when passing through the customs or inspection station. (2) Cotton yarn and its direct woven products manufactured before February 1 that have been shipped from the location of the original yarn mill or textile mill and have arrived at other locations through customs or inspection stations before April 1 can be transported to the interior of the country without supplementing the consolidated tax if the ownership does not belong to the original manufacturer (i.e., other inland areas that are not the location of the original yarn mill or textile mill). However, if the ownership still belongs to the original manufacturer, the consolidated tax must be supplemented (the customs duties that have been paid can be deducted from the consolidated tax) before they can be sold. (3) Cotton yarn and its direct woven products shipped from yarn mills or textile mills and warehouses storing goods from April 1, regardless of whether they are in stock or not, must pay the consolidated tax. (4) Cotton yarn direct products woven by hand from April 1 are allowed to be exempted from inspection of the consolidated tax certificate. However, if they are not made by hand and do not have a cotton yarn tax certificate and the cotton yarn used has not been inspected by the customs, the consolidated tax will still be levied. However, the Federation stated that due to the poor sales of silk in various factories and the heavy taxes levied by the customs, the number of existing yarn and cloth was still large. If the above regulations were followed, they would not be able to bear the burden. Therefore, they again described the difficulties to the Consolidated Tax Office and requested that a further extension be granted to alleviate the difficulties of the merchants. Yesterday, the Consolidated Tax Office replied that it had been approved to extend the time limit by half a month, stating in the original letter, "Upon receipt of your Federation's letter of the 30th, stating that the tax-free sales limit for cotton yarn and its direct woven products in stock on March 31 has expired and that there is still a large amount of stock, please grant a further extension of one month. It has been approved by the Ministry to extend the time limit by half a month, etc., and should be complied with. In addition to separate orders, we are corresponding to inform you to check and inform all manufacturers to be aware."

North Shanghai Over Twenty Silk Factories Went on Strike Yesterday 128

Demanding Restoration of Original Wages

Over Ten Thousand Striking Workers

Yesterday at noon, female workers from the Fengtai Silk Factory at No. 5 Yong'an Lane, West Dayang Bridge, Taiyang Temple, Zhabei, and the Qingfeng Silk Factory on Guangfu Road, went on strike first after their demand for the factory to restore the previous original wages was not met. Around 1 p.m., more than twenty female workers from factories such as Yong'an Silk Factory in the Xinzha district responded in unison and went on strike as a whole, totaling more than sixteen thousand striking workers. The situation is extremely serious. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Reasons for the Strike: Last winter, due to the sluggish silk market, various silk factories in this port negotiated with the workers to calculate workers' wages at 85% of the original rate. Once the market price of each dan of silk exceeded one thousand taels, the original wages would be restored. The longest limit was the end of May of this year. The workers temporarily accepted this without objection. Recently, the selling price of B-grade silk has been above one thousand taels, so the workers began to demand the restoration of the original wages. The day before yesterday afternoon, the Fengtai and Qingfeng silk factories distributed wages still calculated at 85% of the original rate. The workers immediately demanded the restoration of the original price. The factory side stated that the restoration of the price had to wait for the entire city to act uniformly. The workers expressed deep dissatisfaction. At noon yesterday, when it was time to open the factory for lunch, the workers of the two silk factories went on strike first and did not return to the factory. Each factory had more than eight hundred workers.

Response from Various Factories: Around 1 p.m., workers from more than twenty silk factories in the Xinzha District, including Fuchangrun at No. 351 Chang'an Road, Yong'an at No. 468 Meiyuan Road, Xiefeng Baokang at No. 85 Hengfeng Road, Chunmei, Yuanyuan, Longji at No. 799 Chang'an Road, Qichang at No. 530 Chang'an Road, Xie'an at No. 735 Guangfu Road, Tailai at No. 812 Chang'an Road, Baolun at No. 46 Yutong Road, Dingkang, Baisi 2 at No. 37 Hengfeng Road, Baisi 1 at No. 659 Guangfu Road, Dingchangshun, Hengchangxin at No. 246 Hengfeng Road, Shunfengyong at No. 555 Guangfu Road, Fumin at No. 238 Hengfeng Road, Xiechang, Xiexing at No. 225 Chang'an Road, Fuchangtai at No. 695 Chang'an Road, and Yongtaixing at No. 145 Guoqing Road, also responded in unison and went on strike one after another, totaling more than sixteen thousand striking workers.

Factory Precautions: After the labor unrest occurred in the above silk factories, other silk factories such as Hongchun at No. 116 Manzhou Road, Dekang, Lunyuan at No. 6 North Xizang Road, Baojing at No. 5 Wenjisi Tuo Road, and Xuxing, Xukang at No. 54 North Suzhou Road, were deeply afraid that the same incident would occur in their factories. They closed the factory gates and stopped workers from entering and leaving, so no unrest occurred. At 4 p.m., the North District Silk Reeling Industry Union of Zhaofeng Lane, West Baoxing Road, immediately issued an urgent notice advising workers not to strike on their own and to wait quietly for a solution. Therefore, workers from silk factories such as Zhenhe, Jintai, Zhenyu, Qingxiang, Tongli, Hongchang, Junsheng, Fuxing, Lunfu, Shen'an, Fengying, Yushi, and Changyu did not strike.

Management Meeting: After the labor unrest occurred, the silk factories immediately reported to the trade association and immediately held an emergency meeting to find a solution. As of 8 p.m., it was still not over. After the workers went on strike, there were no other actions. It is heard that the union will send representatives to negotiate with the factory to restore the original wages.

Beijing-Shanghai Fourth-Class Passenger Train Departed Earlier 131

Slight Changes in Stops at Various Stations

Previously, the Beijing-Shanghai fourth-class passenger train departed too early and had to stop at every station, often arriving at the terminal station late at night. It is now heard that starting from April 1st, the third and fourth-class express train departing from Shanghai will depart earlier at 5:30 a.m. It will only stop at Huangdu, Kunshan, and Suzhou within the Shanghai-Wuxi section. The third and fourth-class express train departing from Nanjing will also depart earlier at 8 a.m. It will only stop at Suzhou, Kunshan, Anting, and Nanxiang within the Wuxi-Shanghai section. There will also be a third and fourth-class Shanghai-Wuxi regional train that stops at every station for passengers traveling between Shanghai and Wuxi, departing from Shanghai at 7:30 a.m. and from Wuxi at 2:30 p.m. This method is extremely convenient for fourth-class passengers. However, many fourth-class passengers are laborers, and some are illiterate. If the schedule changes, they may not know and may still miss the train. Factory staff and general employers should guide and announce to these workers at any time to fulfill their mutual assistance responsibilities. This can also be a way to care for laborers.

Ship Captain Sends Telegram to Minister Yang 139

Discussing the Lin-Sa-Qiu Case

The case of Lin Zhong, Sa Fuchou, and Qiu Zhenwu being arrested is related to the One-Six Fujian Mutiny. Some people are plotting revenge and falsely accusing them of being communists, and urging Chairman Yang to telegraph Shanghai to arrest them. Yesterday, naval ship captains, considering the feelings of their colleagues, elected representatives to visit them, but they were unable to meet them and returned disappointed. It is now heard that the ship captains have telegraphed and earnestly requested Acting Minister Dai to explain the situation, and also telegraphed Chairman Yang, stating that the three officers are military officers. If they have committed a crime, they should be transferred to the naval department for military trial to show credibility. The telegram from the captains of the ships stationed in Ningbo, Shanghai, and the Yangtze River to the Navy Minister Yang is recorded below: To Minister Yang of the Fujian Provincial Government: News reports state that Sa Fuchou, Lin Zhong, Qiu Zhenwu, and others are involved in the assassination of Zhang, and it is also said that they are communists who negotiated with the Japanese consul in Shanghai and were arrested on the Jiuri ship in Changsha and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for detention. We, the undersigned, were shocked and bewildered to hear the news. The captains of the ships stationed in Ningbo, Shanghai, and the Yangtze River have been sending telegrams to inquire about the truth. However, Sa and others are either naval generals whose military status has not been removed, or they have been following his command for many years. If they have committed a crime, the military law is in place. How could they be humiliated to this extent? We were confused and puzzled. Yesterday, we read the news and learned that the Fujian Provincial Government submitted a request to the Central Government to arrest Sa and others because they were suspected of conspiring with the One-Six Mutiny in Fujian Province. Your Excellency is well aware of this case. Yesterday, the captains of the ships went to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to request to see Sa and others to express our condolences and fulfill our comradeship, but the authorities refused, stating that they were ordered not to allow visits. We returned disappointed. We believe that Your Excellency leads the entire army and also leads the provincial government. All members of the entire army love and support Your Excellency, and Your Excellency will certainly protect them. The situation of Sa and others being arrested as reported has chilled the hearts of those in the military. Your Excellency must also have deep feelings. We hope that Your Excellency will immediately telegraph the Shanghai authorities to send Sa and others back to the navy for handling in order to protect the military's reputation and remedy the situation. We, the undersigned, are relying on Your Excellency's protection and are driven by loyalty. We dare not remain silent in danger. We deeply hope that Your Excellency will make a decisive decision and accept our loyal advice. We await orders with trepidation.

Ninth Meeting of Various Industry Tax Rules Conference 140

Any Business Tax Exceeding Two Per Thousand Will Be Rejected

The Shanghai Municipal Various Industry Trade Association Tax Rules Committee held its ninth meeting yesterday afternoon. Committee members Shen Weiting, Sun Choucheng, Jiang Zhigang, Zheng Chengqing, Zhu Wenqi, Mao Chunpu, Shao Baoxing, Luo Qinghua, and others, more than ten people in total, attended. Chairman Zheng Chengqing presided over the meeting and reported on incoming and outgoing documents, followed by a discussion of the resolutions as follows: (1) Case on how to handle the business tax rate exceeding two per thousand in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. It was resolved that any exceeding two per thousand will be rejected and submitted to the Ministry of Finance of the National Government for revision. (2) Case on how to express the fact that Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are collecting 4.2% for the wholesale industry, which violates the Ministry's order. It was resolved to submit to the Ministry of Finance of the National Government for correction. (3) Case on how to handle the report that the Shanghai Municipal business tax rate has been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for review. It was resolved that the Shanghai Municipal business tax rate has not been agreed upon by the Chamber of Commerce representatives and various industries in advance. If any exceed two per thousand, they will be rejected and the Ministry of Finance will be requested to review it carefully. (4) Case on whether to refuse investigation before the Municipal business tax rate has been approved by the Ministry of Finance. It was resolved to notify various industry associations to refuse to fill out the report upon receiving the notification from this association. Finally, other important cases were discussed and the meeting adjourned.

Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Transportation Industry Meeting 142

Discussion on Remedies for the Railway Bureau's Increased Fees

The Shanghai Municipal Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Transportation Industry Association, due to the Railway Bureau's 20% increase in freight rates on March 16, has been holding joint meetings of representatives from transportation industry associations at various stations along the entire line from April 1st to 3rd to address the various difficulties in freight and passenger transport caused by the increased freight rates and to request the ministry and bureau to consider reducing the increase. Yesterday (the 1st) was the first day of the joint meeting to discuss remedies. The joint meeting began at 10 a.m. The representatives entered the meeting to discuss remedies. First, Shen Huiquan, chairman of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Association, reported that the Railway Bureau's increase in freight rates on March 16 made train transport more expensive than ship transport for merchants. The Shanghai-Hangzhou line is different from other lines in nature. At present, it is in the midst of competition between water and land transport. Requests for lower freight rates were made at both the two-way business meeting and the Ministry of Railways business meeting. Now that the price reduction has not been implemented, the current increase seems to be out of touch with commercial sentiment, and merchants are increasingly switching to ship transport, especially for North-South goods, grains, and kerosene. The industry has suffered a loss, and the Railway Bureau's income has also been reduced. Therefore, representatives from the same industry were gathered today to discuss remedies. First, a comparison table of the difference in the number of freight transportations between train transport and ship transport will be submitted to the ministry, and the opinion letters submitted by the representatives will be discussed one by one. The result of the discussion is scheduled to be reviewed starting at 2 p.m. (today). The meeting adjourned at 3 p.m.

Result of Negotiation between Labor and Management on the Sale of the Sanxin Yarn Factory 144

Total of 85,000 Foreign Dollars

However, Various Workers Expressed Dissatisfaction

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau was ordered to handle the sale of the Sanxin Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road. The third mediation was convened at 1 p.m. yesterday. After a long period of consultation, it was learned that the labor and management had resolved the issue through oral negotiation. The details of yesterday's situation are recorded separately below:

Number of Attendees: At 1 p.m. yesterday, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau convened the third mediation of the three parties: Factory owner Sheng Zecheng, manager Sheng Yulin of the Sanxin Yarn Factory, Rong Zongjing, general manager of the Xin Xin Yarn Factory, and the Third Special District Cotton Textile Industry Union. Sheng Yulin sent a letter stating that he had resigned and would not attend. Zhu Guangcheng, the authorized representative of the shareholders of the Sanxin Yarn Factory, Rong Zongjing, the new buyer, also sent an authorized representative to attend. Tian Sanzi, Gu Lansheng, He Baojin, Hou Jiahai, and more than 20 representatives of workers from 18 departments of the factory attended the meeting on behalf of the Third Special District Cotton Textile Industry Union. Section member Xu Zhi chaired the meeting, and Zhu Guilin recorded the minutes.

Mediation Situation: After a long period of inquiry by the chairman, it was learned that the labor-management dispute had been resolved orally by Sun Hecai, the general representative of the workers, and Zhu Guangcheng, the shareholder representative of the factory, through repeated negotiations. The factory will issue a total of 85,000 yuan to all factory staff and workers. Approximately 100 staff members will receive 60,000 yuan, and more than 4,000 workers will receive 25,000 yuan. The chairman said that since the matter has been resolved through negotiation, there is no need for further mediation.

Worker Dissatisfaction: Representatives of workers from various departments expressed dissatisfaction with the decisions made by the factory and the general representative of the workers. The reason is that when cooperating with the staff, General Representative Sun announced to everyone that if the negotiation results in a subsidy, staff and workers will be distributed equally. Now, each staff member can get 600 yuan, while each worker only gets 4.5 yuan. They believe this is unfair and demand a renegotiation. The chairman instructed the representatives to consult with General Representative Sun first to discuss the distribution plan. If a solution cannot be found, they can submit a request to the bureau. At the same time, he instructed the management representative not to make the payment before the distribution issue is resolved. The management representative Zhu Guang responded that the Social Affairs Bureau would be notified before the payment is made.

All Staff Members of the Anti-Drug Association's Executive Department Express Opinions on the Bai Case 146

Letter to the Standing Committee

Since the Bai Zhiying drug trafficking case was reported, all staff members of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association's Executive Department have not made any reports to the outside world because the truth of the case is unclear. However, due to frequent inquiries from all parties, all staff members have had to make a fair statement to dispel doubts. Yesterday, they sent a letter to the association's Standing Committee, advocating that public and private boundaries should be clarified and the truth should be investigated. The letter is excerpted below: "To Chairman Wang and all members of the Standing Committee: Since the Bai case occurred, the association has advocated that public and private matters should be clarified. The Standing Committee has resolved four important measures, especially the second measure, which states that 'Before the truth is clear, all internal and external affairs of the association will be jointly responsible by the four members designated by the Standing Committee, Wang Jingqi, Li Denghui, Zhong Ketuo, and Cai Rudong, and Chen Hongjun will be appointed as acting director-general.' This clear measure on the task of the former director-general is most important. We, the undersigned, believe that this is the only fair proposal and must always be thoroughly appreciated and not be tolerated or changed in the slightest. If the public and private affairs of this case are not clear and we listen to Mr. Huang and still come to the meeting and use the name of the entire association as a tool for personal expression, it will inevitably lead to misunderstandings from the outside world. We, the undersigned, have served for many years and are greatly concerned, and the life of the association is at stake. We hope that the National Government will immediately conduct a thorough investigation of the case. If the facts are true, the association should, in the spirit it has always held, earnestly request the National Government to deal with it severely in accordance with the law in order to maintain the association's inherent reputation. We hope that the public opinion of the entire executive department will not be ignored." Guomin She reported that the 18 branches of the 3rd district of this city held the 29th party member congress the day before yesterday, advocating strict punishment in the Bai case, but because the truth is unclear, four party members were specially assigned to conduct a secret investigation. In order to take into account the achievements of the Anti-Drug Association in its efforts to combat drugs over the past few years and to implement President Sun's anti-drug legacy, two measures were unanimously decided upon: (1) The National Anti-Drug Association should clearly dismiss Huang Jia-hui, the director-general and husband of Bai Zhiying, before the truth of the case is clear. (2) The National Anti-Drug Association should issue a statement in the newspaper stating that the case is a personal action of Huang Jia-hui and Bai Zhiying and has absolutely nothing to do with the Anti-Drug Association in order to avoid misunderstandings from the outside world. The above measures have been handed over to the executive committee of the branch for implementation.

Local News Two

Appeal Hearing for the Cai Fulin Kidnapping Case 147

The Bandits Continue to Shift Blame

Cai Fulin Recounts His Kidnapping Experience

Closing Arguments Concluded, Sentencing Scheduled

Cai Fulin, a comprador for the British American Tobacco Company, was kidnapped near Avenue Road and Hart Road on March 14th of the year before last and ransomed for 30,000 yuan. Subsequently, the police arrested several kidnappers, including Zhang Hongxiang, Jin Changshou, Zhang Jinsheng, Zhang Qian, and Chen Wu. After a trial by the Special District Court, Zhang Hongxiang and others were sentenced to death, while the remaining individuals received prison sentences. Zhang Qian was acquitted, and Chen Wu received a life sentence. Later, the police, dissatisfied with the acquittal of Zhang Qian, who was suspected of knowingly assisting the bandits by delivering food in their lair, filed an appeal. Chen Wu also hired a lawyer to appeal. The Higher Court held a hearing yesterday.

Zhang Qian: According to Zhang Qian's testimony, she is 22 years old, from Zhenjiang, and resides at No. 7 Jiaozhou Road, Shanghai. Zhang Jinsheng is her lover. Her former husband died on April 26th of the 18th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1929]. She has been with Zhang for less than a year and does not know Zhang Hongxiang. Because it was Zhang Jintang's daughter's first-month celebration, her lover took her to a feast. Zhang Jintang's wife asked her to help with housework at her home, so she stayed there for about five days. At that time, Jintang's wife said that a friend from the military was sick in the pavilion and asked her to deliver food daily, only delivering it to the side of the staircase and not entering the room. She only went to the sun deck to dry clothes and saw a person sleeping on the bed. She claims she knew nothing about the kidnapping case.

Chen Wu: Chen Wu testified that she has a friendly relationship with Jin Changshou. Jin borrowed 3,000 taels and 5,000 yuan from a person surnamed Xia, with her husband acting as guarantor. Because the debt was overdue, her husband went to Songjiang. She went to the Great Eastern Hotel to demand repayment. At that time, she only heard Jin Changshou tell Zhang Jintang that Cai Fulin had a lot of family wealth, about two to three hundred thousand, and suggested they think of a way [to get it]. She only heard this from the side and did not participate in the discussion or receive any stolen money. The reason she was falsely accused was because she had quarreled with Jin Changshou over debt collection and stopped patronizing Lao Jie Fu, Yang Qing He, and other establishments, leading to a grudge, etc.

Jin Changshou: Jin Changshou stated that since he has already been convicted, everything he says is truthful. He testified that Chen Wu is a relative who seeks money and legal assistance. He does not owe Chen Wu any money; it was the person surnamed Xia who owed. He did not discuss the Cai kidnapping with Chen Wu. His previous testimony was based on what Zhang Jinsheng said because he was suffering from hemoptysis and afraid of police procedures. Therefore, his first statement to the police was entirely based on Zhang Jinsheng. His second statement in court was true. He did not know Zhang Jintang before; he met him at a gambling den through Chen Wu. Later, he lent money to Zhang Jintang and went to the Great Eastern Hotel to collect it. He denies ever saying to Zhang Jintang that Cai Fulin had two to three hundred thousand, etc.

Cai Fulin: According to Cai Fulin, after being kidnapped, he was first taken to Avenue Joffre, then to Avenue du Cycle for one day each, and then to No. 86 Zhoujiazui Road. It was a one-up, one-down house with a nanny, a caretaker, and children. There were three people guarding him with two handguns, which they carried interchangeably, sometimes holding them, sometimes hiding them on their bodies. Zhang Qian delivered food many times, bringing it into the room. On the surface, she looked like a nanny. He cannot be certain whether she participated in the kidnapping, but it is difficult to say she knew nothing. Inside the lair, he only read newspapers and was treated very comfortably, etc.

Zhang Jinsheng: Zhang Jinsheng testified that he worked as a waiter at Quan Jia Fu. Jin Changshou came to eat, which is how they met. Later, he learned that Jin ran the Great Eastern Hotel and often went there to play when getting an oil massage. One day, he saw a note demanding ransom money from Cai Fulin. When the matter was exposed, he was forced to write letters four times. However, he did not see Chen Wu at the time. Zhang Jintang told him at the police station that if he did not implicate Chen Wu, Chen Wu would have him shot, so he had no choice but to falsely accuse her, etc. The judges repeatedly questioned the defendants and allowed the defense lawyers and police lawyers to cross-examine. After a final court ruling, the closing arguments concluded and sentencing was scheduled for March 8th.

Sixteen Extortion Cases 148

The Extortion Letters are in Official Style

The Handwriting is Elegant and Bears an Official Seal

Hu Yigu was Also Extorted

Liu Ronggen, a Chinese detective from the Jing'an Temple police station, along with Wang Zhusheng, and Bao Tan Shan Huihai, previously arrested three members of an extortion gang: Zhou Wangzuo, Guo Xianggao, and Tang Shuisheng. Bai Zhongqi, the Chinese Detective Chief of the Huisi police station, also apprehended one of their accomplices, Zhang Jinhai, and brought him to the Special District Court for trial and detention. After a thorough investigation, the detective discovered that the defendants had colluded to write threatening letters in the Public Concession, demanding huge sums of money from wealthy households in at least sixteen cases. This is unprecedented. Moreover, the letters used by these individuals were in official style, the handwriting was elegant, and they bore an official seal. The letters were in the name of the "National Salvation Martial Arts Association" and generally stated that they were short of military funds and were temporarily borrowing several thousand yuan from the recipient. The wording was often similar. The details of each case are recorded below: (1) On January 25th of this year, attempted to defraud Chen Junbao of 5,000 yuan at No. 197 Muir Road; (2) In April of the 18th year of the Republic [i.e., 1929], attempted to defraud Dr. Yun Tieqiao of 500 yuan at No. 278 Yunnan Road; (3) In February of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Shen Yuzi, the owner of the Shi Ming Electric Light Store, of 200 yuan at No. 1305 Beijing Road; (4) In December of the 17th year [i.e., 1928], attempted to defraud Dr. Shen Zhuoru of a large sum at No. 42 Guling Road; (5) In March of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Wang Gaosheng, the owner of a hardware store, of 3,000 yuan at No. 289 Avenue Foch; (6) In May of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Tian Yushu of 2,000 yuan at No. 694 Shanhai Pass Road; (7) In January of this year, attempted to defraud Ye Zengshou of a large sum at No. 369 Yulin Road; (8) In January of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Dr. Xu Yi of a large sum at No. 713 Dixwell Road; (9) In December of the 17th year, attempted to defraud Dr. Sun Yusheng of a large sum at No. 1594 North Chengdu Road; (10) In December of the 17th year, extorted 30 yuan from Fan Xiaoling at No. 407 Jiujiang Road; (11) In June of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Dr. Zhu Zongzeng of a large sum at No. 70 Yunnan Road; (12) In November of the 17th year, attempted to defraud Guo Zibin of a large sum at No. 101 New Dagu Road; (14) In June/July of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Zhang Jianqing of a large sum at No. 762 East Yalu Road; (15) In May of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Gu Disan, a comprador for the Korean Bank, of a large sum at No. 41 Gordon Road; (16) In June of the 18th year, attempted to defraud Hu Yigu, the head of the civil division of the Jiangsu Higher Court, of 3,000 yuan at No. 432 Dixwell Road, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge Zitan presided over a continued hearing in the second criminal court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin began by presenting the case, stating that during the previous court session, the defendant Tang Shuisheng confessed that he was the informant in this case (i.e., the reporter) and had previously reported Zhang Jinhai and others to Chinese Detective Chief Bai Zhongqi. Now that Detective Chief Bai has also arrived in court, he should be questioned. Detective Chief Bai then testified that Tang was indeed an informant in the case. He said that he was unaware of Tang's arrest until Tang's wife came to his office crying, saying that he had been detained by the Jing'an Temple police station. Judge Ge then questioned the defendants and ordered them to be taken back into custody, with a rescheduled hearing on the afternoon of the 14th of this month.

Cultural Theft Case 149

Wei Juezhong's Identity Verification Photos with Inscriptions Stolen

Hoping the Thief Will Return Them to Complete His Writing

The New Voice Society received a letter yesterday from the Nanyang Cultural Undertakings Department of National Jinan University, stating that Mr. Wei Juezhong, who traveled extensively throughout Nanyang by bicycle the year before last, had returned to China last year and published his work, "Southern Wilderness Peoples." Because he preferred tranquility, he moved from Shanghai to No. 932 Zhenru Railway Station Road to write and prepare for a trip to the Northeast.

Unexpected Theft: Unfortunately, on the morning of March 10th, Mr. Wei went to Shanghai for business. When he returned in the afternoon, his door had been pried open by a thief. His clothes and money were all gone. Mr. Wei's travel identification, autographs from celebrities from various places, photos of local people taken along the way, and many manuscripts about Nanyang were also stolen.

Overwhelmed with Grief: Mr. Wei was overwhelmed with grief. He wrote many notices about the lost items, posted them on busy streets, hoping that the thief would have a change of heart and return the results of his many years of travel in Nanyang. However, to this day, there is still no news. Mr. Wei is restless and seems to be developing a nervous disorder. According to Mr. Wei, all civilized countries in the world take great care to protect travelers. Although the theft occurred in broad daylight and was reported to the police, the stolen items have not been recovered. He sincerely hopes that the local authorities can quickly help him recover his important documents and travel identification so that he can complete his great undertaking of traveling the world and prevent overseas Chinese in Nanyang from viewing the country as a dangerous place, hesitating to come forward.

Room Renters are Robbers 150

Women First Rent the Room

Robbers Search Each Household

A daytime robbery occurred yesterday, the 1st, at 3:30 PM at No. 157, Section West, Shanhai Lane, Shanhai Pass Road. The details of the investigation are recorded below:

Several Families Reside in One House: No. 157 Shanhai Lane, Shanhai Pass Road, is a three-story stone-framed building along the road. The sublessor, surnamed Yang, works at the China Bookstore and lives in the west wing downstairs. He rents the east wing to a family surnamed Chen and the pavilion in the west wing to a family surnamed Zhang. Two other families live upstairs, both of whom are engaged in business. The men are all away, leaving only women inside.

Young Girl Opens the Door: The sublessor had posted a rental notice on the door because there were vacant rooms upstairs. A woman came to inquire about renting the rooms the week before last, but it did not work out. Yesterday (the 1st) at 3:30 PM, a young, fashionably dressed girl knocked on the door claiming to be interested in renting a room. The old woman surnamed Yang, the sublessor, opened the door and led her upstairs to look around. After briefly inquiring about the rent, the girl left. Then, three robbers wearing long gowns and mandarin jackets, speaking with northern accents, each carrying a handgun, broke into the west wing downstairs and searched it thoroughly. They first silenced the old woman surnamed Yang, forcibly removing a gold bracelet and two gold rings from her hand. They then went to the Chen family in the east wing, holding a gun and forcing them into the back room. They snatched a jewelry box containing emerald jade ornaments (worth about several hundred yuan) and removed a six-qian gold ring from the maid's hand. Then they went to the Zhang family in the pavilion, removing two gold bracelets from the housewife's hand and stealing 55 yuan in cash from her friend surnamed Wang.

A Bullet is Dropped: The robbers, fearing trouble because the search took too long, did not dare go upstairs. They hurriedly carried the stolen goods and fled. One of the robbers dropped a bullet from his handgun, but they did not have time to pick it up. They fled through the front door. After the robbers left, the victims picked up the bullet and saw the number 32 written on it.

Victims Report to the Police, Requesting Arrest: The total loss for the three families was approximately 2,000 yuan. The victims filed a report with the Xinzha police station, requesting an arrest. The police chief immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate and begin the arrest.

A Robber Spits Out a Gold Ring 151

The Stolen Goods are in the Thief's Mouth

Yesterday morning at about 10 AM, a Yangzhou woman named Hu Wang was returning from buying vegetables on Ninghe Road when a robber suddenly approached her from behind near the entrance of Maijia Lane and snatched a pair of gold rings from her ears. She cried out for help, and a guard named Liu Shuyin from the nearby Fourth Post heard her and immediately gave chase. Her husband, Mr. Hu, also heard the commotion and joined in the pursuit. They managed to restrain the robber. The robber, realizing his predicament, secretly put the stolen goods in his mouth. Officer Liu searched him thoroughly but could not find any evidence. Mr. Hu was furious because he knew that the robber had stolen his wife's gold earrings and was unable to recover the stolen goods. He immediately slapped the robber in the face. The robber cried out in pain, opening his mouth, and a pair of gold rings fell out. They took the robber and the stolen goods back to the third section of the first district, where Section Chief Jin interrogated him. The robber confessed his name was Zhang Agen, 24 years old, a local resident lodging at Tianfu Inn on Second Ma Road in the Public Concession. He also admitted to robbing the woman's gold rings. He was ordered to prepare a document and hand over the person and stolen goods to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Anhui Series Publishing House Established 154

Anhui has suffered from natural disasters and banditry in recent years, and society is bleak. However, people from Anhui are striving for cultural development, such as the construction of Anhui University, the compilation of the Anhui Gazetteer, and the advancement of the Oriental Cultural Society. Recently, they have jointly planned to establish the Anhui Series Publishing House to publish the Anhui Series. Many people have recognized and invested in the project, led by Mr. Cheng Linsheng, China's only great collector of ancient bronzes, who has provided a large sum of money for start-up costs. The establishment meeting was held last month at Cheng Linsheng's residence on Jing'an Temple Road, and Jiang Tonghou was elected as the director and Wang Mengzou as the clerk. Yesterday, the editorial review committee met at Cheng Yansheng's residence on Avenue Foch, and Xu Jiyu and Huang Binhong (both also serving as standing members for collecting versions), Chen Ziyan, Hong Zecheng, Zhang Yanchang, Cheng Linsheng (also serving as standing members for economics), Xu Jingren, Cheng Yansheng (also serving as standing members for public relations), Li Guangjiong, Li Mugong, Li Weihou, Wu Jingtian (also serving as standing members for documentation), Zhou Meiquan, Wang Yitang, and Hu Pu'an were elected as the 15 members of the editorial review committee. Various regulations were passed, methods for engraving books were discussed, and it was proposed to hire book collectors and collators from the province and abroad as honorary members of the association to provide guidance. Anhui's classics, philology, mathematics, literature, philosophy, and art all hold important positions in history. In the future, the publication of the series will make a great contribution to scholarship, which can be anticipated. The office is now located at No. 271 Avenue Foch in this city.

A Glimpse of the Qipu Road Robbery 155

Six Robbers Ascend the Stairs Three Times

The Ma Family's Loss is Fortunately Not Huge

The home of a Mr. Ma, an employee of the Shenchang Foreign Firm, at No. 622 Dongpuyi Lane, Qipu Road, south of the District Court, was robbed yesterday morning at 9:30 AM. Although the loss was less than a thousand gold, the location is next to the court and police station. The robbers dared to be so rampant in broad daylight, showing extreme disregard for the law. The details of the robbery are described below:

Mr. Ma's residence is a two-story building. Yesterday morning at 9:30 AM, only Mr. Ma's wife, mother-in-law, and a maid were at home in the living room, preparing the vegetables they had bought. Mr. Ma had already gone to work, and his children were at school. Six robbers in short clothes arrived at Dongpuyi Lane. One robber guarded the back door of Mr. Ma's residence in the second alley, and the other five entered the first alley. Leaving one robber to loiter at the entrance as a lookout, the other four knocked on the front door of Mr. Ma's residence, claiming to need to discuss business with Mr. Ma. Mr. Ma's wife told the maid to open the door. The four robbers swarmed in and immediately closed the door tightly. One robber stood leaning against the door, and another robber pulled out a handgun and a foot-long white blade, holding one in each hand. They first warned the maid not to make a sound, then addressed Mr. Ma's wife as "Master Ma's wife" and claimed to be there to borrow money. Mr. Ma's wife said that her family was poor and asked for forgiveness. Mr. Ma's mother-in-law also said to the robbers that they were near the court and asked them not to be rash. The robbers showed displeasure upon hearing this, claiming that they were not interfering with public affairs and were willing to die for their cause. They then stared at Mr. Ma's wife's neck, suspecting that she might be wearing gold necklaces or lockets. Mr. Ma's wife immediately unbuttoned her collar. Seeing that there was nothing, the robbers snatched a jade hairpin from her hair. They also wanted to rob the gold earrings from her ears, but Mr. Ma's wife said that they were trivial and asked them to leave them alone. The robbers then gave up. They asked Mr. Ma's wife or the maid to lead them upstairs, but neither was willing. Therefore, the three robbers went upstairs themselves, entered the room, and rummaged through the chests and cabinets. They only found a gold watch worth 60 yuan and over 100 yuan in cash. They went downstairs and whispered to each other, then said that the amount was not enough to cover their travel expenses. They went back upstairs and searched again, but did not find anything valuable. However, they still wanted to leave, then stopped for a third time and went upstairs, taking a fox fur coat, a cat fur coat, and a long lined robe, which the three robbers put on. Because there were still account books and blank checks on the table, they wrapped them up in a piece of white cloth. They also took a vintage gold button from Mr. Ma's wife's clothing and a box of copper coins and miscellaneous currency (which were kept for the children as toys) from the desk. They then calmly said to Mr. Ma's wife that they originally intended to take Mr. Ma with them, but they spared him because his family depended on him for a living. They told her to carefully observe their faces if she wanted to recognize them. While speaking, they drove Mr. Ma's wife, the maid, and his elderly, visually impaired mother-in-law behind a screen and used electrical wire to tie up the screen before shouting and fleeing through the front door. After a long time, Mr. Ma's wife and the others went upstairs to check and saw that the boxes and belongings were still neatly arranged by the robbers. They estimated that the stolen goods were worth no less than several hundred gold. Just as they were about to file a report with the police, the Huisi police station, which had already received a report, immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives in cars to Mr. Ma's house to investigate. They then notified all police stations to pursue and arrest the robbers and punish them. There were police posts within dozens of yards on all sides, showing the robbers' audacity was truly outrageous.

Russian Woman Seems to Have a Nervous Disorder 162

Her Actions and Words are Incomprehensible

Will Be Sent to Harbin Hospital for Treatment

It was previously discovered that a Russian woman named Shuai Si Peilin had engaged in certain behaviors, and the Municipal Council dispatched police officers to closely monitor her. The woman used this as a pretext to write to the Chief of Police, demanding compensation of 100,000 yuan for her losses. She also wrote to Yang, the district chief of the police department, and Ma Hao, a Western detective, demanding a monthly allowance of 600 yuan. She also falsely accused Detective Ma of stealing her clothes and jewelry. Her actions were similar to those of someone with a nervous disorder. The police arrested the Russian woman and sent her to the Special District Court, which ordered her to be examined by a doctor from the Municipal Council. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu brought Shuai Si Peilin to court again for a continued hearing. Police lawyer Wei Yinde presented the examination report from Dr. Smith, the director of the Municipal Council Hospital, stating that according to Dr. Smith's diagnosis, she was indeed suffering from mental illness. If the woman were allowed to remain in Shanghai, she would pose a danger to the public. The police are currently planning to send her to the mental hospital of the China Eastern Railway in Harbin. The expenses will be borne by the police. Shuai Si Peilin then stated through an interpreter that the evidence presented by the police to arrest her was insufficient to prove her guilt, so her arrest was illegal. She did not have a mental illness, and the police's statements were not credible. Judge Xu said that she had previously reported stolen items, but the police department's investigation proved that her report was false. Her actions constituted false accusation, which is a criminal offense. The case still requires Dr. Smith to be summoned to court to inquire about her condition, so the hearing must be postponed. The police then took the Russian woman away for detention.

Yu Hechang's Wife Recovery Case 163

Summary of Yesterday's Second Hearing

Seven-Day Deadline for the Wei Mother and Daughter to Hand Over the Person

Yu Hechang, a 45-year-old businessman from Nantong with some savings, married Wei Zhaodi, the daughter of Wei Chen, from Ningbo several years ago. The relationship between the couple was good after the marriage. However, since last year, his wife was seduced by her younger sister, Wei Amao, to commit adultery with others and colluded to abscond, resulting in a loss of more than 1,300 yuan. Her whereabouts are still unknown. Yu Hechang filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai Local Court. Since the defendant lived in the Public Concession, he hired lawyer Li Junhuan to file a complaint with the Special District Court. The first hearing was held in the third court on March 2nd. Yesterday afternoon was the second hearing, presided over by Judge Cheng Shangfeng. The defendant, Wei Sanmao, and the defendant's mother, Wei Chen, were both present in court to await questioning. First, the plaintiff, Yu Hechang, stated the circumstances of his wife's seduction by Wei Sanmao and the reasons for his accusation. Wei Sanmao denied seducing her sister, and Wei Chen also claimed that she did not know anything about her daughter's adultery and absconding. After the interrogation, the court ordered that the case be adjourned for one week and that the defendants Wei Sanmao and Wei Chen hand over Wei Zhaodi within one week. At the same time, the plaintiff must also make further inquiries to facilitate the hearing. The court then adjourned.

Car Actually Crashes Tram Off the Rails 166

Tram Hits Japan Tourist Bureau

Passengers Slightly Startled, Fortunately No One Killed

Offending Car Owned by Ma Yinchu

Parking on Roadside Suffers Undeserved Disaster

At 11:10 last night, a car on Nanjing Road at the Jiangxi Road intersection crashed into a tram, causing it to derail and narrowly escaping a major disaster. A No. 7 tram was traveling west on Nanjing Road. About twenty yards from the intersection of Jiangxi Road, a No. 11749 Packard sedan, also traveling west, attempted to overtake the tram. Unexpectedly, a No. 1163 black Packard sedan was parked on the side of the road in front of the New Comfort House. As the No. 7 tram was passing the parked car, the No. 11749 car sped forward between the two vehicles. However, the car body was huge and the road narrow, making it difficult to pass. The car crashed into the tram with great force, causing it to derail. The tram was unable to brake and, after derailing, moved forward in a semicircle, passing in front of the New Comfort House and the Sino-American Bookstore until it stopped in front of the Japan International Tourist Bureau at No. 80 Nanjing Road. The iron gate of the Japan International Tourist Bureau was broken by the tram, and a large piece of glass in the door and window area was also shattered. The iron gate of the tram was also damaged by the No. 11749 car. The front and rear right fenders of the offending car were completely destroyed in the collision with the tram, while the left rear fender was damaged in the collision with the parked No. 3163 car. The No. 1163 car also suffered damage to the rear right fender. A No. 1546 Nash sedan, which was following closely behind the No. 11749 car, was also slightly damaged in the collision. The accident occurred late at night, and fortunately, there were fewer pedestrians and vehicles on the road, so no one was injured. The three cars involved and their drivers were taken to the Central Police Station by the patrolmen. The offending car, No. 11749, is owned by Ma Yinchu.

Kodak World Photography Grand Competition with US$100,000 in Prizes 168

Kodak's Generous Move

Over 8,000 Yuan in Total Prizes for China

Kodak Company, located at 24 Yuanmingyuan Road, has long been renowned throughout the country for its photographic materials. In order to promote the popularization of photography and encourage the interest of photographers, they are holding an unprecedented world photography grand competition. By spending only a small amount of time submitting photos, there is hope of winning a prize. However, only amateur photographers are allowed to join the competition in order to cultivate their love of beauty. The competition in China has already started collecting entries at the beginning of February this year and is scheduled to end at the end of May. The more entries submitted, the better. The amount of prizes is also unusually high compared to previous competitions. They are listed as follows: (1) Category Prizes: Divided into six categories: children, landscapes, sports, still life, informal portraits, and livestock. Each category has a first prize of 200 yuan, a second prize of 100 yuan, a third prize of 50 yuan, a fourth prize of five winners at 10 yuan each, and a fifth prize of fifty winners at 2 yuan each. (2) Provincial and Regional Prizes: Divided into twenty-two provinces and regions. Each province and region has a first prize of 100 yuan, a second prize of 30 yuan, and a third prize of thirty-five winners at 2 yuan each. (3) National Grand Prize: One prize of 1,000 silver dollars and a medal. The person who wins the first prize in each category will be a participant in the World Photography Grand Competition. The winners of the World Category Grand Prizes will each receive US$1,000. The best in the six categories will receive a special prize of US$10,000 and a trophy. Therefore, one photo has the potential to win consecutive prizes up to 1,300 Chinese currency and US$11,000, which is truly an unprecedented generous move in the photography world. It is said that since the announcement, those who have heard the news are joining like mushrooms after rain, with exceptional enthusiasm. Anyone who wants to know the details of the competition can write to the company for them.

Dispute Among New Workers on the Gonghe Steamer 171

Temporarily Allowed on Board, Work as Usual

Chen Bonian, the new comprador of the Ewo Company's Gonghe Steamer, declared when he boarded the ship at 2:00 p.m. on the 31st of last month to take over that all thirty-eight new workers, including Chen Jinlan, would be dismissed and ordered to leave the ship. All the new workers had no choice but to petition the Social Affairs Bureau. The bureau sent Wang Bing to the Gonghe Steamer at the Shuntai Wharf to negotiate with the new comprador, resulting in (1) the thirty-eight new workers being temporarily allowed on board to work as usual, and (2) waiting for the Hankou Municipal Government to arbitrate. Thus, the dispute among the new workers was temporarily resolved.

Qingxiang Bureau of Shanghai County Begins Investigating Ships 172

The Qingxiang Bureau of Shanghai County is actively carrying out the Qingxiang work within a short time limit in order to complete it on schedule. At the moment, the investigation of ships is extremely important for Qingxiang, so Bureau Chief Yan Ken ordered that it begin on April 2nd (today). In addition to ordering all sub-bureaus to comply and implement the order, he also sent a letter to District Chief Xu of the Water Police First District yesterday, requesting that he order his subordinates to assist in the matter.

Jiangyu Steamer Sailed Yesterday 173

Mediation Process

Details of the strike that occurred on the Jiangyu Steamer have been reported in previous newspapers. The cause of the incident was that the General Bureau transferred the boatswain to Tianjin, causing a misunderstanding among the workers who suspected that he had been dismissed. They petitioned the union to retain him, but the bureau stated that the order had already been issued and it was difficult to change. Therefore, the strike occurred. After receiving the news, the General Bureau immediately sent Nan Zhan Inspection Director Liu Zhen, Deputy Director Qiao Songren, and Bei Zhan Inspection Director Xu Songyue to the Seamen's Union to negotiate several times before they finally understood. However, in order to maintain its authority, the bureau had temporarily agreed to serve on the ship. The union secretaries believed that the tone of the reply was vague and feared that it would change halfway, so they asked Du Yuesheng to mediate. The result was satisfactory. That evening, the ship loaded all the goods accumulated at the dock and sailed at 8:00 a.m. the next morning.

Edward Cannot Be Reinstated

The Public Works Department of the Public Settlement held its regular board meeting last night. Regarding the issue of the suspended Director-General Edward, it was decided that Edward would continue to receive his original salary until the expiration of his contract next year, but he could not be reinstated.

Meeting Record of the Fenghua Fellow Association 175

The Fenghua Fellow Association in Shanghai held a temporary plenary committee meeting yesterday. He Pinglong and others were present. Yu Hualong was elected as chairman. The agenda items were (1) a letter from the Fenghua County Magistrate requesting donations for the repair of the county jail. It was passed that the Ningbo Fellow Association in Shanghai and the Dinghai Fellow Association in Shanghai should each be invited to send personnel to conduct on-site investigations, after which a joint meeting would be held to deliberate on the matter; (3) a letter from Chen Bowei stating that he had been falsely accused of fraud and sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment by the Special District Court. He had already appealed and requested assistance in forwarding the letter to the appellate court to prove the facts. It was resolved to prepare a letter to the appellate court to prove the facts; (4) Wu Zhihao proposed that the association should prepare the Fenghua Water Conservancy Association regarding the Fenghua water conservancy matter. It was resolved to do so and to invite Mr. Zhuang Songfu to be the preparatory director of the Fenghua Water Conservancy Association, with Wu Zhihao and Yu Hualong as his deputies, and to invite Chen Zhonggao, He Shaoyu, He Shaoting, He Pinglong, Zhu Meixuan, Kang Nian, Wang Shijia, and more than twenty others to be committee members. The meeting adjourned at six o'clock.
